widely accepted)</span></span></td>\n</tr>\n<tr class="mergedtoprow">\n<th scope="row">Time zone</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">EST</a> <span class="nowrap">(<a scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:BS" title="ISO 3166-2:BS">BS</a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/.bs" title=".bs">.bs</a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">\n<ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_bahoffbox"><b><a href="#ref_bahoffbox">^</a></b></span> Also referred to as <i>Bahamian dialect</i> or <i>Bahamianese</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>The Bahamas</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">b</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: \'a\' in \'about\'">\xc9\x99</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="\'h\' in \'hi\'">h</span><span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/: \'a\' in \'father\'">\xc9\x91\xcb\x90</span><span title="\'m\' in \'my\'">m</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: \'a\' in \'about\'">\xc9\x99</span><span title="\'z\' in \'zoom\'">z</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">\xc2\xa0(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Bahamas.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a>\xc2\xa0</span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/72/En-us-Bahamas.ogg" title="En-us-Bahamas.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>), known officially as the <b>Commonwealth of The Bahamas</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/Archipelagic_state" title="Archipelagic state">archipelagic state</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_Archipelago" title="Lucayan Archipelago">Lucayan Archipelago</a>. It consists of more than 700 <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cay" title="Cay">cays</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islet" title="Islet">islets</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, and is located north of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> (<a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>), northwest of the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>, southeast of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US" title="US">US</a> state of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, and east of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a>. The capital is <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">Nassau</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/New_Providence" title="New Providence">New Providence</a>. The designation of "the Bahamas" can refer either to the country or to the larger island chain that it shares with the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>. As stated in the mandate/manifesto of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bahamas_Defence_Force" title="Royal Bahamas Defence Force">Royal Bahamas Defence Force</a>, the Bahamas territory encompasses 470,000\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup> (180,000\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) of ocean space.</p>\n<p>The Bahamas is the site of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Columbus</a>\' first landfall in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> in 1492. At that time, the islands were inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_people" title="Lucayan people">Lucayan</a>, a branch of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawakan" title="Arawakan">Arawakan</a>-speaking <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Taino</a> people. Although the Spanish never colonised The Bahamas, they shipped the native Lucayans to slavery in Hispaniola. The islands were mostly deserted from 1513 until 1648, when <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> colonists from <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> settled on the island of <a href="/wiki/Eleuthera" title="Eleuthera">Eleuthera</a>.</p>\n<p>The Bahamas became a <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown colony</a> in 1718, when the British clamped down on <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American War of Independence</a>, the Crown resettled thousands of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Loyalists" title="American Loyalists">American Loyalists</a> in the Bahamas; they brought their slaves with them and established plantations on land grants. Africans constituted the majority of the population from this period. The slave trade was abolished by the British in 1807; slavery in the Bahamas was abolished in 1834. The Bahamas became a haven for freed African slaves; the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> resettled Africans here liberated from illegal slave ships, <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">American slaves</a> and Seminoles escaped here from Florida, and the government freed American slaves carried on United States domestic ships that had reached the Bahamas due to weather. Today, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Bahamians" title="Afro-Bahamians">Afro-Bahamians</a> make up nearly 90% of the population.</p>\n<p>The Bahamas became an independent <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a> in 1973, retaining the British monarch, then and currently <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, as its head of state. In terms of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> per capita, The Bahamas is one of the richest countries in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> (following the United States and Canada), with an economy based on tourism and finance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Etymology"><span links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name <i>Bahamas</i> is mostly likely derived from either the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> <i><span lang="tnq">ba ha ma</span></i> ("big upper middle land"), which was a term for the region used by the indigenous Native Americans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> or possibly from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> <i><span lang="es">baja mar</span></i> ("shallow water or sea" or "<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bajamar" title="es:Bajamar">low tide</a>") reflecting the shallow waters of the area. Alternatively, it may originate from <i><span lang="tnq"><a href="/wiki/Guanahani" title="Guanahani">Guanahani</a></span></i>, a local name of unclear meaning.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A peculiarity of the name is that the word <i>The</i> is a formal part of the abbreviated name and is, therefore, capitalised. So in contrast to "the Congo" and "the United Kingdom", it is proper to write "The Bahamas".</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>\n</td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(July 2017)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Bahamas" title="History of the Bahamas">History of the Bahamas</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Landing_of_Columbus_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1971" data-file-width="3000" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/220px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/330px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg/440px-Landing_of_Columbus_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Landing_of_Columbus_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA depiction of Columbus\' first landing, claiming possession of the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> for Spain in <a href="/wiki/Caravel" title="Caravel">caravels</a>; the <i><a href="/wiki/Ni%C3%B1a" title="Ni\xc3\xb1a">Ni\xc3\xb1a</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Pinta_(ship)" title="Pinta (ship)">Pinta</a></i>, on Watling Island, an island of The Bahamas that the natives called <a href="/wiki/Guanahani" title="Guanahani">Guanahani</a> and that he named <i>San Salvador</i>, on 12 October 1492.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Taino</a> people moved into the uninhabited southern Bahamas from <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> around the 11th century, having migrated there from South America. They came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_people" title="Lucayan people">Lucayan people</a>. An estimated 30,000 Lucayan inhabited the Bahamas at the time of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>\' arrival in 1492.</p>\n<p>Columbus\'s first landfall in the New World was on an island he named San Salvador (known to the Lucayan as <i><a href="/wiki/Guanahani" title="Guanahani">Guanahani</a></i>). Some researchers believe this site to be present-day <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador_Island" title="San Salvador Island">San Salvador Island</a> (formerly known as Watling\'s Island), situated in the southeastern Bahamas. An alternative theory holds that Columbus landed to the southeast on <a href="/wiki/Samana_Cay" title="Samana Cay">Samana Cay</a>, according to calculations made in 1986 by <i><a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_(magazine)" title="National Geographic (magazine)">National Geographic</a></i> writer and editor <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Judge" title="Joseph Judge">Joseph Judge</a>, based on Columbus\'s log. Evidence in support of this remains inconclusive. On the landfall island, Columbus made first contact with the Lucayan and exchanged goods with them.</p>\n<p>The Spanish forced much of the Lucayan population to Hispaniola for use as forced labour. The slaves suffered from harsh conditions and most died from contracting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" title="Infectious disease">diseases</a> to which they had no <a href="/wiki/Immunity_(medical)" title="Immunity (medical)">immunity</a>; half of the Taino died from <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The population of the Bahamas was severely diminished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 1648, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleutherian_Adventurers" title="Eleutherian Adventurers">Eleutherian Adventurers</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/William_Sayle" title="William Sayle">William Sayle</a>, migrated from Bermuda. These English Puritans established the first permanent European settlement on an island which they named <a href="/wiki/Eleuthera" title="Eleuthera">Eleuthera</a>\xe2\x80\x94the name derives from the Greek word for freedom. They later settled <a href="/wiki/New_Providence" title="New Providence">New Providence</a>, naming it Sayle\'s Island after one of their leaders. To survive, the settlers <a href="/wiki/Wrecking_(shipwreck)#The_Bahamas" title="Wrecking (shipwreck)">salvaged goods from wrecks</a>.</p>\n<p>In 1670, <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">King Charles II</a> granted the islands to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lords_Proprietors" title="Lords Proprietors">Lords Proprietors</a> of the Carolinas in North America. They rented the islands from the king with rights of trading, tax, appointing <a href="/wiki/Governor#British_Empire_and_Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Governor">governors</a>, and administering the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anglican_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anglican-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1684 Spanish <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">corsair</a> Juan de Alcon <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Charles_Town" title="Raid on Charles Town">raided the capital</a>, Charles Town (later renamed <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">Nassau</a>). In 1703, a joint Franco-Spanish expedition <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Nassau" title="Raid on Nassau">briefly occupied</a> the Bahamian capital during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>.</p>\n<h3><span id="18th\xe2\x80\x9319th_centuries"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="18th.E2.80.9319th_centuries">18th\xe2\x80\x9319th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 18th\xe2\x80\x9319th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Escaping_To_Freedom_In_The_Bahamas_sign_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Escaping_To_Freedom_In_The_Bahamas_sign_01.jpg/220px-Escaping_To_Freedom_In_The_Bahamas_sign_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Escaping_To_Freedom_In_The_Bahamas_sign_01.jpg/330px-Escaping_To_Freedom_In_The_Bahamas_sign_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Escaping_To_Freedom_In_The_Bahamas_sign_01.jpg/440px-Escaping_To_Freedom_In_The_Bahamas_sign_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Escaping_To_Freedom_In_The_Bahamas_sign_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSign at <a href="/wiki/Bill_Baggs_Cape_Florida_State_Park" title="Bill Baggs Cape Florida State Park">Bill Baggs Cape Florida State Park</a> commemorating hundreds of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">African-American</a> slaves who escaped to freedom in the early 1820s in the Bahamas</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>During proprietary rule, the Bahamas became a haven for <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">pirates</a>, including the infamous <a href="/wiki/Blackbeard" title="Blackbeard">Blackbeard</a> (<i>circa</i> 1680\xe2\x80\x931718). To put an end to the \'<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pirates%27_republic" title="Pirates\' republic">Pirates\' republic</a>\' and restore orderly government, Britain made the Bahamas a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_overseas_territories" title="British overseas territories">crown colony</a> in 1718 under the royal governorship of <a href="/wiki/Woodes_Rogers" title="Woodes Rogers">Woodes Rogers</a>. After a difficult struggle, he succeeded in suppressing piracy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> In 1720, Rogers led local <a href="/wiki/Militia" title="Militia">militia</a> to drive off a <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nassau_(1720)" title="Battle of Nassau (1720)">Spanish attack</a>.</p>\n<p>During the American War of Independence in the late 18th century, the islands became a target for American naval forces under the command of Commodore <a href="/wiki/Esek_Hopkins" title="Esek Hopkins">Esek Hopkins</a>. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">US Marines</a> occupied the capital of Nassau for a <a href="/wiki/Fortnight" title="Fortnight">fortnight</a>.</p>\n<p>In 1782, following the British defeat at <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" title="Siege of Yorktown">Yorktown</a>, a Spanish fleet appeared off the coast of Nassau. The city <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capture_of_The_Bahamas_(1782)" title="Capture of The Bahamas (1782)">surrendered without a fight</a>. Spain returned possession of the Bahamas to Britain the following year, under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris</a>. Before the news was received, however, the <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_the_Bahamas_(1783)" title="Capture of the Bahamas (1783)">islands were recaptured</a> by a small British force led by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Deveaux" title="Andrew Deveaux">Andrew Deveaux</a>.</p>\n<p>After American independence, the British resettled some 7,300 <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">Loyalists</a> with their slaves in the Bahamas, and granted land to the planters to help compensate for losses on the continent. These Loyalists, who included Deveaux, established plantations on several islands and became a political force in the capital. European Americans were outnumbered by the African-American slaves they brought with them, and ethnic Europeans remained a minority in the territory.</p>\n<p>In 1807, the British abolished the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">slave trade</a>, followed by the United States the next year. During the following decades, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> intercepted the trade; they resettled in the Bahamas thousands of Africans liberated from slave ships.</p>\n<p>In the 1820s during the period of the <a href="/wiki/Seminole_Wars" title="Seminole Wars">Seminole Wars</a> in Florida, hundreds of American slaves and African Seminoles escaped from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Florida" title="Cape Florida">Cape Florida</a> to the Bahamas. They settled mostly on northwest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andros_Island" title="Andros Island">Andros Island</a>, where they developed the village of Red Bays. From eyewitness accounts, 300 escaped in a mass flight in 1823, aided by Bahamians in 27 <a href="/wiki/Sloop" title="Sloop">sloops</a>, with others using canoes for the journey. This was commemorated in 2004 by a large sign at <a href="/wiki/Bill_Baggs_Cape_Florida_State_Park" title="Bill Baggs Cape Florida State Park">Bill Baggs Cape Florida State Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nps_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-nps-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Some of their descendants in Red Bays continue African Seminole traditions in basket making and grave marking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The United States\' <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a>, which administers the National <a href="/wiki/Underground_Railroad" title="Underground Railroad">Underground Railroad</a> Network to Freedom, is working with the African Bahamian Museum and Research Center (ABAC) in Nassau on development to identify Red Bays as a site related to American slaves\' search for freedom. The museum has researched and documented the African Seminoles\' escape from southern Florida. It plans to develop interpretive programs at historical sites in Red Bay associated with the period of their settlement in the Bahamas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 1818,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> the Home Office in London had ruled that "any slave brought to the Bahamas from outside the <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a> would be manumitted." This led to a total of nearly 300 slaves owned by US nationals being freed from 1830 to 1835.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-horne103_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-horne103-25">[25]</a></sup> The American slave ships <i>Comet</i> and <i>Encomium</i> used in the United States domestic <a href="/wiki/Coastwise_slave_trade" title="Coastwise slave trade">coastwise slave trade</a>, were wrecked off Abaco Island in December 1830 and February 1834, respectively. When wreckers took the masters, passengers and slaves into Nassau, customs officers seized the slaves and British colonial officials freed them, over the protests of the Americans. There were 165 slaves on the <i>Comet</i> and 48 on the <i>Encomium</i>. Britain finally paid an indemnity to the United States in those two cases in 1855, under the Treaty of Claims of 1853, which settled several compensation cases between the two nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debates_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-debates-27">[27]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Slavery was <a href="/wiki/Slavery_Abolition_Act_1833" title="Slavery Abolition Act 1833">abolished in the British Empire</a> on 1 August 1834. After that British colonial officials freed 78 American slaves from the <i><a href="/wiki/Enterprise_(slave_ship)" title="Enterprise (slave ship)">Enterprise</a></i>, which went into Bermuda in 1835; and 38 from the <i>Hermosa</i>, which wrecked off Abaco Island in 1840.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The most notable case was that of the <i>Creole</i> in 1841: as a result of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_revolt" title="Slave revolt">slave revolt</a> on board, the leaders ordered the American brig to Nassau. It was carrying 135 slaves from Virginia destined for sale in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>. The Bahamian officials freed the 128 slaves who chose to stay in the islands. The <i><a href="/wiki/Creole_case" title="Creole case">Creole</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Creole_case" title="Creole case">case</a> has been described as the "most successful slave revolt in U.S. history".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-williams_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-williams-29">[29]</a></sup></p>\n<p>These incidents, in which a total of 447 slaves belonging to US nationals were freed from 1830 to 1842, increased tension between the United States and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Great Britain</a>. They had been co-operating in patrols to suppress the international slave trade. But, worried about the stability of its large domestic slave trade and its value, the United States argued that Britain should not treat its domestic ships that came to its colonial ports under duress, as part of the international trade. The United States worried that the success of the <i>Creole</i> slaves in gaining freedom would encourage more slave revolts on merchant ships.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Duke_of_Windsor_(1945).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="744" data-file-width="620" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/The_Duke_of_Windsor_%281945%29.jpg/170px-The_Duke_of_Windsor_%281945%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/The_Duke_of_Windsor_%281945%29.jpg/255px-The_Duke_of_Windsor_%281945%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/The_Duke_of_Windsor_%281945%29.jpg/340px-The_Duke_of_Windsor_%281945%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Duke_of_Windsor_(1945).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Edward_VIII" title="Edward VIII">Edward VIII</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Windsor" title="Duke of Windsor">Duke of Windsor</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Bahamas" title="Governor of the Bahamas">Governor of the Bahamas</a> from 1940 to 1945</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In August 1940, after his abdication of the British throne, the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Windsor" title="Duke of Windsor">Duke of Windsor</a> was installed as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Bahamas" title="Governor of the Bahamas">Governor of the Bahamas</a>, arriving with his wife, the <a href="/wiki/Wallis_Simpson" title="Wallis Simpson">Duchess</a>. Although disheartened at the condition of Government House, they "tried to make the best of a bad situation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Windsor_installed_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Windsor_installed-30">[30]</a></sup> He did not enjoy the position, and referred to the islands as "a third-class British colony".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>\n<p>He opened the small local parliament on 29 October 1940. The couple visited the "Out Islands" that November, on <a href="/wiki/Axel_Wenner-Gren" title="Axel Wenner-Gren">Axel Wenner-Gren</a>\'s yacht, which caused controversy;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Windsor_opened_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Windsor_opened-32">[32]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Foreign_Office" title="British Foreign Office">British Foreign Office</a> strenuously objected because they had been advised (mistakenly) by United States intelligence that Wenner-Gren was a close friend of the <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> commander <a href="/wiki/Hermann_G%C3%B6ring" title="Hermann G\xc3\xb6ring">Hermann G\xc3\xb6ring</a> of Nazi Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Windsor_opened_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Windsor_opened-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Duke was praised at the time for his efforts to combat poverty on the islands. A 1991 biography by Philip Ziegler, however, described him as contemptuous of the Bahamians and other non-European peoples of the Empire. He was praised for his resolution of civil unrest over low wages in <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">Nassau</a> in June 1942, when there was a "full-scale riot".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Windsor_unrest_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Windsor_unrest-34">[34]</a></sup> Ziegler said that the Duke blamed the trouble on "mischief makers \xe2\x80\x93 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communists" title="Communists">communists</a>" and "men of Central European <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> descent, who had secured jobs as a pretext for obtaining a deferment of draft".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ziegler_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-ziegler-35">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The Duke resigned the post on 16 March 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-matthew_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-matthew-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Windsor_resigned_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Windsor_resigned-37">[37]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Second_World_War">Post-Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Post-Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sir._Roland_Symonette_Park_Sign.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="452" data-file-width="604" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Sir._Roland_Symonette_Park_Sign.jpg/220px-Sir._Roland_Symonette_Park_Sign.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Sir._Roland_Symonette_Park_Sign.jpg/330px-Sir._Roland_Symonette_Park_Sign.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Sir._Roland_Symonette_Park_Sign.jpg/440px-Sir._Roland_Symonette_Park_Sign.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sir._Roland_Symonette_Park_Sign.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSign at the entrance of the Sir Roland Symonette Park in <a href="/wiki/North_Eleuthera" title="North Eleuthera">North Eleuthera</a> district commemorating Sir <a href="/wiki/Roland_Theodore_Symonette" title="Roland Theodore Symonette">Roland Theodore Symonette</a>, the Bahamas\' first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Bahamas" title="Prime Minister of the Bahamas">Premier</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Modern political development began after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. The first political parties were formed in the 1950s. The British Parliament authorised the islands as internally self-governing in 1964, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Roland_Symonette" title="Sir Roland Symonette">Sir Roland Symonette</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/United_Bahamian_Party" title="United Bahamian Party">United Bahamian Party</a>, as the first Premier.</p>\n<p>A new constitution granting the Bahamas internal autonomy went into effect on 7 January 1964.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In 1967, <a href="/wiki/Lynden_Pindling" title="Lynden Pindling">Lynden Pindling</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Liberal_Party" title="Progressive Liberal Party">Progressive Liberal Party</a>, became the first native born Premier of the majority native Bahamian colony; in 1968 the title of the position was changed to <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Bahamas" title="Prime Minister of the Bahamas">Prime Minister</a>. In 1968, Pindling announced that the Bahamas would seek full independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> A new constitution giving the Bahamas increased control over its own affairs was adopted in 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_House_of_Lords" title="British House of Lords">British House of Lords</a> voted to give the Bahamas its independence on 22 June 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Charles" title="Prince Charles">Prince Charles</a> delivered the official documents to <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Bahamas" title="Prime Minister of the Bahamas">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Lynden_Pindling" title="Lynden Pindling">Lynden Pindling</a>, officially declaring the Bahamas a fully independent nation on 10 July 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> It joined the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Milo_Butler" title="Sir Milo Butler">Sir Milo Butler</a> was appointed the first <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_the_Bahamas" title="Governor-General of the Bahamas">Governor-General of the Bahamas</a> (the official representative of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Queen Elizabeth II</a>) shortly after independence. The Bahamas joined the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> on 22 August 1973,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> and it joined the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> on 18 September 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Based on the twin pillars of tourism and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Offshore_finance" title="Offshore finance">offshore finance</a>, the Bahamian economy has prospered since the 1950s. Significant challenges in areas such as education, health care, housing, international <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narcotics_trafficking" title="Narcotics trafficking">narcotics trafficking</a> and illegal immigration from Haiti continue to be issues.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Bahamas" title="University of the Bahamas">University of The Bahamas</a> (UB) is the national higher education/tertiary system. Offering baccalaureate, masters and associate degrees, UB has three campuses, and teaching and research centres throughout the Bahamas. The University of the Bahamas was chartered on November 10, 2016</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Bahamas" title="Geography of the Bahamas">Geography of the Bahamas</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bahamas_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="720" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Bahamas_2009.jpg/220px-Bahamas_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Bahamas_2009.jpg/330px-Bahamas_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Bahamas_2009.jpg/440px-Bahamas_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bahamas_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe Bahamas from space. <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> <a href="/wiki/Aqua_(satellite)" title="Aqua (satellite)">Aqua</a> satellite image, 2009</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The country lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/20th_parallel_north" title="20th parallel north">20\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/28th_parallel_north" title="28th parallel north">28\xc2\xb0N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/72nd_meridian_west" title="72nd meridian west">72\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/80th_meridian_west" title="80th meridian west">80\xc2\xb0W</a>.</p>\n<p>In 1864, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Bahamas" title="Governor of the Bahamas">Governor of the Bahamas</a> reported that there were 29 islands, 661 cays, and 2,387 rocks in the colony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The closest island to the United States is <a href="/wiki/Bimini" title="Bimini">Bimini</a>, which is also known as the gateway to the Bahamas. The island of <a href="/wiki/Abaco_Islands" title="Abaco Islands">Abaco</a> is to the east of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bahama" title="Grand Bahama">Grand Bahama</a>. The southeasternmost island is <a href="/wiki/Inagua" title="Inagua">Inagua</a>. The largest island is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andros_Island" title="Andros Island">Andros Island</a>. Other inhabited islands include <a href="/wiki/Eleuthera" title="Eleuthera">Eleuthera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cat_Island,_Bahamas" title="Cat Island, Bahamas">Cat Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rum_Cay" title="Rum Cay">Rum Cay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long_Island,_Bahamas" title="Long Island, Bahamas">Long Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador_Island" title="San Salvador Island">San Salvador Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ragged_Island,_Bahamas" title="Ragged Island, Bahamas">Ragged Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acklins" title="Acklins">Acklins</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crooked_Island_(Bahamas)" title="Crooked Island (Bahamas)">Crooked Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exuma" title="Exuma">Exuma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berry_Islands" title="Berry Islands">Berry Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mayaguana" title="Mayaguana">Mayaguana</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">Nassau</a>, capital city of the Bahamas, lies on the island of <a href="/wiki/New_Providence" title="New Providence">New Providence</a>.</p>\n<p>All the islands are low and flat, with ridges that usually rise no more than 15 to 20\xc2\xa0m (49 to 66\xc2\xa0ft). The highest point in the country is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Alvernia" title="Mount Alvernia">Mount Alvernia</a> (formerly Como Hill) on Cat Island. It has an elevation of 63 metres (207\xc2\xa0ft).</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_wilma_devastation.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hurricane_wilma_devastation.jpg/220px-Hurricane_wilma_devastation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hurricane_wilma_devastation.jpg/330px-Hurricane_wilma_devastation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hurricane_wilma_devastation.jpg/440px-Hurricane_wilma_devastation.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_wilma_devastation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nDamaged homes in the Bahamas in the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a> in 2005</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>To the southeast, the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>, and three more extensive submarine features called <a href="/wiki/Mouchoir_Bank" title="Mouchoir Bank">Mouchoir Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silver_Bank" title="Silver Bank">Silver Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Navidad_Bank" title="Navidad Bank">Navidad Bank</a>, are geographically a continuation of the Bahamas.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Castaway_Cay">Castaway Cay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Castaway Cay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Castaway_Cay" title="Castaway Cay">Castaway Cay</a></div>\n<p>Disney Has it own private island in the Bahamas called <a href="/wiki/Castaway_Cay" title="Castaway Cay">Castaway Cay</a> It is located near Great Abaco Island and was formerly known as Gorda Cay. In 1997, The Walt Disney Company purchased a 99-year land lease for the cay from the Bahamian government, set to expire in 2096</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Bahamas#Climate" title="Geography of the Bahamas">Geography of the Bahamas \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Climate</a></div>\n<p>The climate of the Bahamas is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_savannah_climate" title="Tropical savannah climate">tropical savannah climate</a> or <i>Aw</i> according to <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a>. The low latitude, warm tropical <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>, and low <a href="/wiki/Elevation" title="Elevation">elevation</a> give the Bahamas a warm and winterless climate. As such, there has never been a frost or freeze reported in the Bahamas, although every few decades low temperatures can fall below 10\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (50\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) for a few hours when a severe cold outbreak comes off the North American mainland. There is only an 8\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C difference between the warmest month and coolest month in most of the Bahama islands. As with most tropical climates, seasonal rainfall follows the sun, and summer is the wettest season. The Bahamas are often sunny and dry for long periods of time, and average more than 3,000 hours or 340 days<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> of sunlight annually.</p>\n<p>Tropical storms and hurricanes can on occasion impact the Bahamas. In 1992, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Andrew" title="Hurricane Andrew">Hurricane Andrew</a> passed over the northern portions of the islands, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Floyd" title="Hurricane Floyd">Hurricane Floyd</a> passed near the eastern portions of the islands in 1999.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; text-align:center; class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Bahamas Platform, which includes the Bahamas, Southern Florida, Northern Cuba, the Turks and Caicos, and the <a href="/wiki/Blake_Plateau" title="Blake Plateau">Blake Plateau</a>, formed about 150 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megaannum" title="Megaannum">Ma</a>, not long after the formation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic" title="North Atlantic">North Atlantic</a>. The 6.4\xc2\xa0km thick <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestones</a>, which predominately make up The Bahamas, date back to the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a>. These limestones would have been deposited in shallow seas, assumed to be a stretched and thinned portion of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Plate" title="North American Plate">North American continental crust</a>. Sediments were forming at about the same rate as the crust below was sinking due to the added weight. Thus, the entire area consisted of a large marine plain with some islands. Then, at about 80 Ma, the area became flooded by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>. This resulted in the drowning of the Blake Plateau, the separation of The Bahamas from Cuba and Florida, the separation of the southeastern Bahamas into separate banks, the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Cay_Sal_Bank" title="Cay Sal Bank">Cay Sal Bank</a>, plus the <a href="/wiki/Bahama_Banks" title="Bahama Banks">Little and Great Bahama Banks</a>. Sedimentation from the "carbonate factory" of each bank, or <a href="/wiki/Atoll" title="Atoll">atoll</a>, continues today at the rate of about 2\xc2\xa0cm per <a href="/wiki/Kyr" title="Kyr">kyr</a>. <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">Coral reefs</a> form the "retaining walls" of these atolls, within which <a href="/wiki/Oolite" title="Oolite">oolites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pellets_(petrology)" title="Pellets (petrology)">pellets</a> form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sealey_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sealey-50">[50]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Coral growth was greater through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tertiary_(geology)" title="Tertiary (geology)">Tertiary</a>, until the start of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ice_Ages" title="Ice Ages">Ice Ages</a>, and hence those deposits are more abundant below a depth of 36 m. In fact, an ancient extinct reef exists half a km seaward of the present one, 30 m below sea level. Oolites form when oceanic water penetrate the shallow banks, increasing the temperature about 3\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C and the salinity by 0.5 per cent. <a href="/wiki/Cementation_(geology)" title="Cementation (geology)">Cemented</a> <a href="/wiki/Ooid" title="Ooid">ooids</a> are referred to as grapestone. Additionally, giant <a href="/wiki/Stromatolite" title="Stromatolite">stromatolites</a> are found off the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exuma_Cays" title="Exuma Cays">Exuma Cays</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sealey_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sealey-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:22,29\xe2\x80\x9330</sup></p>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_level_change" title="Sea level change">Sea level changes</a> resulted in a drop in sea level, causing wind blown oolite to form <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sand_dune" title="Sand dune">sand dunes</a> with distinct <a href="/wiki/Cross-bedding" title="Cross-bedding">cross-bedding</a>. Overlapping dunes form oolitic ridges, which become rapidly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithified" title="Lithified">lithified</a> through the action of rainwater. Most islands have ridges ranging from 30 to 45 m, though Cat Island has a ridge 60 m in height. The land between ridges is conducive to the formation of lakes and swamps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sealey_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sealey-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:41\xe2\x80\x9359,61\xe2\x80\x9364</sup></p>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solution_weathering" title="Solution weathering">Solution weathering</a> of the limestone results in a "Bahamian <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">Karst</a>" topography. This includes <a href="/wiki/Pothole_(geology)" title="Pothole (geology)">potholes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_hole" title="Blue hole">Blue holes</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Dean%27s_Blue_Hole" title="Dean\'s Blue Hole">Dean\'s Blue Hole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sinkhole" title="Sinkhole">sinkholes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beachrock" title="Beachrock">beachrock</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Bimini_Road" title="Bimini Road">Bimini Road</a> ("pavements of Atlantis"), <a href="/wiki/Caliche" title="Caliche">limestone crust</a>, caves due to the lack of rivers, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_caves" title="Sea caves">sea caves</a>. Several blue holes are aligned along the South Andros <a href="/wiki/Fault_(geology)" title="Fault (geology)">Fault</a> line. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidal_flat" title="Tidal flat">Tidal flats</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tidal_creek" title="Tidal creek">tidal creeks</a> are common, but the more impressive drainage patterns are formed by troughs and canyons such as <a href="/wiki/Great_Bahama_Canyon" title="Great Bahama Canyon">Great Bahama Canyon</a> with the evidence of <a href="/wiki/Turbidity_current" title="Turbidity current">turbidity currents</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turbidite" title="Turbidite">turbidite</a> deposition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sealey_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sealey-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:33\xe2\x80\x9340,65,72\xe2\x80\x9384,86</sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Bahamas" title="Politics of the Bahamas">Politics of the Bahamas</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BahamianParliamentPanorama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2534" data-file-width="7181" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/BahamianParliamentPanorama.jpg/300px-BahamianParliamentPanorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/BahamianParliamentPanorama.jpg/450px-BahamianParliamentPanorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/BahamianParliamentPanorama.jpg/600px-BahamianParliamentPanorama.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BahamianParliamentPanorama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Bahamas" title="Parliament of the Bahamas">Bahamian Parliament</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">Nassau</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Bahamas is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> headed by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> in her role as Queen of the Bahamas. Political and legal traditions closely follow those of the United Kingdom and the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a>. The Bahamas is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a>, retaining the Queen as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> (represented by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Governors-General_of_the_Bahamas" title="List of Governors-General of the Bahamas">Governor-General</a>).</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">Legislative power</a> is vested In a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>, which consists of a 38-member <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_the_Bahamas" title="House of Assembly of the Bahamas">House of Assembly</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a>), with members elected from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" title="Plurality voting system">single-member districts</a>, and a 16-member <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliament_of_The_Bahamas#Senate" title="Parliament of The Bahamas">Senate</a>, with members appointed by the Governor-General, including nine on the advice of the Prime Minister, four on the advice of the <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition" title="Leader of the Opposition">Leader of Her Majesty\'s Loyal Opposition</a>, and three on the advice of the Prime Minister after consultation with the Leader of the Opposition. The House of Assembly carries out all major legislative functions. As under the Westminster system, the Prime Minister may dissolve Parliament and call a general election at any time within a five-year term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_Minister" title="Prime Minister">Prime Minister</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and is the leader of the party with the most seats in the House of Assembly. <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">Executive power</a> is exercised by the Cabinet, selected by the Prime Minister and drawn from his supporters in the House of Assembly. The current Governor-General is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dame_Marguerite_Pindling" title="Dame Marguerite Pindling">Dame Marguerite Pindling</a>, and the current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_government_of_the_Bahamas" title="List of heads of government of the Bahamas">Prime Minister</a> is <a href="/wiki/The_Right_Honourable" title="The Right Honourable">The Rt. Hon.</a> <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Minnis" title="Hubert Minnis">Hubert Minnis</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" title="Member of Parliament">M.P.</a>.</p>\n<p>Constitutional safeguards include <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">press</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">worship</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_movement" title="Freedom of movement">movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_association" title="Freedom of association">association</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_the_Bahamas" title="Judiciary of the Bahamas">Judiciary of the Bahamas</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature. Jurisprudence is based on <a href="/wiki/English_law" title="English law">English law</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Bahamas has a <a href="/wiki/Two-party_system" title="Two-party system">two-party system</a> dominated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centre-left" title="Centre-left">centre-left</a> <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Liberal_Party" title="Progressive Liberal Party">Progressive Liberal Party</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centre-right" title="Centre-right">centre-right</a> <a href="/wiki/Free_National_Movement" title="Free National Movement">Free National Movement</a>. A handful of splinter parties have been unable to win election to parliament. These parties have included the <a href="/wiki/Bahamas_Democratic_Movement" title="Bahamas Democratic Movement">Bahamas Democratic Movement</a>, the Coalition for Democratic Reform, Bahamian Nationalist Party and the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_National_Alliance_(Bahamas)" title="Democratic National Alliance (Bahamas)">Democratic National Alliance</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Bahamas" title="Foreign relations of the Bahamas">Foreign relations of the Bahamas</a></div>\n<p>The Bahamas has strong bilateral relationships with the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, represented by an ambassador in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_Commissioner" title="High Commissioner">High Commissioner</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. The Bahamas also associates closely with other nations of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM).</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Armed forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bahamas_Defence_Force" title="Royal Bahamas Defence Force">Royal Bahamas Defence Force</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hmbsnassau.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Hmbsnassau.jpg/220px-Hmbsnassau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Hmbsnassau.jpg/330px-Hmbsnassau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Hmbsnassau.jpg/440px-Hmbsnassau.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hmbsnassau.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nHMBS Nassau (P-61)</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Its military is the Royal Bahamas Defence Force (the RBDF), the navy of the Bahamas which includes a land unit called Commando Squadron (Regiment) and an Air Wing (Air Force). Under the Defence Act, the RBDF has been mandated, in the name of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_The_Bahamas" title="Elizabeth II of The Bahamas">Queen</a>, to defend the Bahamas, protect its territorial integrity, patrol its waters, provide assistance and relief in times of disaster, maintain order in conjunction with the law enforcement agencies of the Bahamas, and carry out any such duties as determined by the National Security Council. The Defence Force is also a member of the Caribbean Community (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caricom" title="Caricom">CARICOM</a>)\'s Regional Security Task Force.</p>\n<p>The RBDF came into existence on 31 March 1980. Their duties include defending the Bahamas, stopping <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade" title="Illegal drug trade">drug smuggling</a>, illegal immigration and poaching, and providing assistance to mariners. The Defence Force has a fleet of 26 coastal and inshore patrol craft along with 3 aircraft and over 1,100 personnel including 65 officers and 74 women.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_Bahamas" title="Local government in the Bahamas">Local government in the Bahamas</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Districts_of_the_Bahamas_(Labeled).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="856" data-file-width="825" height="363" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Districts_of_the_Bahamas_%28Labeled%29.png/350px-Districts_of_the_Bahamas_%28Labeled%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Districts_of_the_Bahamas_%28Labeled%29.png/525px-Districts_of_the_Bahamas_%28Labeled%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Districts_of_the_Bahamas_%28Labeled%29.png/700px-Districts_of_the_Bahamas_%28Labeled%29.png 2x" width="350"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Districts_of_the_Bahamas_(Labeled).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nDistricts of the Bahamas</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The districts of the Bahamas provide a system of local government everywhere except <a href="/wiki/New_Providence" title="New Providence">New Providence</a> (which holds 70% of the national population), whose affairs are handled directly by the central government. In 1996, the Bahamian Parliament passed the "Local Government Act" to facilitate the establishment of Family Island Administrators, Local Government Districts, Local District Councillors and Local Town Committees for the various island communities. The overall goal of this act is to allow the various elected leaders to govern and oversee the affairs of their respective districts without the interference of Central Government. In total, there are 32 districts, with elections being held every five years. There are 110 Councillors and 281 Town Committee members are elected to represent the various districts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Each Councillor or Town Committee member is responsible for the proper use of public funds for the maintenance and development of their constituency.</p>\n<p>The Bahamas uses <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">drive-on-the-Left</a> traffic rules throughout the Commonwealth.</p>\n<p>The districts other than New Providence are:</p>\n<div style="font-size:95%;">\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style=";border-spacing:0;background:transparent;">\n<tr style="vertical-align:top;">\n<td style="width:40em;;{{{col1style}}};">\n<div style="margin-left: 2em">\n<ol>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Acklins" title="Acklins">Acklins</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Berry_Islands" title="Berry Islands">Berry Islands</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bimini" title="Bimini">Bimini</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Point_(Bahamas)" title="Black Point (Bahamas)">Black Point</a>, <a Abaco">Central Abaco</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Central_Andros" title="Central Andros">Central Andros</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Central_Eleuthera" title="Central Eleuthera">Central Eleuthera</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Freeport,_Bahamas" title="Freeport, Bahamas">City of Freeport, Grand Bahama</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Crooked_Island,_Bahamas" title="Crooked Island, Bahamas">Crooked Island</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/East_Grand_Bahama" title="East Grand Bahama">East Grand Bahama</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Exuma" title="Exuma">Exuma</a></li>\n<li><a
