title="Harbour Island (Bahamas)">Harbour Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eleuthera" title="Eleuthera">Eleuthera</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hope_Town" title="Hope Town">Hope Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abaco_Islands" title="Abaco Islands">Abaco</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inagua" title="Inagua">Inagua</a></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n</td>\n<td style="width:1.25em;"></td>\n<td style="width:40em;;{{{col2style}}};">\n<div style="margin-left: 2em">\n<ol start="17">\n<li><a href="/wiki/Long_Island,_Bahamas" title="Long Island, Bahamas">Long Island</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mangrove_Cay" title="Mangrove Cay">Mangrove Cay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andros,_Bahamas" title="Andros, Bahamas">Andros</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mayaguana" title="Mayaguana">Mayaguana</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Moore%27s_Island" title="Moore\'s Island">Moore\'s Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abaco_Islands" title="Abaco Islands">Abaco</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/North_Abaco" title="North Abaco">North Abaco</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/North_Andros" title="North Andros">North Andros</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/North_Eleuthera" title="North Eleuthera">North Eleuthera</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ragged_Island,_Bahamas" title="Ragged Island, Bahamas">Ragged Island</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rum_Cay" title="Rum Cay">Rum Cay</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/San_Salvador_Island" title="San Salvador Island">San Salvador</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/South_Abaco" title="South Abaco">South Abaco</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/South_Andros" title="South Andros">South Andros</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/South_Eleuthera" title="South Eleuthera">South Eleuthera</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Wells" title="Spanish Wells">Spanish Wells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eleuthera" title="Eleuthera">Eleuthera</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/West_Grand_Bahama" title="West Grand Bahama">West Grand Bahama</a></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_flag">National flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: National flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Bahamas" title="Flag of the Bahamas">Flag of the Bahamas</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Bahamas.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="600" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Flag_of_the_Bahamas.svg/170px-Flag_of_the_Bahamas.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Flag_of_the_Bahamas.svg/255px-Flag_of_the_Bahamas.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Flag_of_the_Bahamas.svg/340px-Flag_of_the_Bahamas.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Bahamas.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nNational flag of the Bahamas</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The colours embodied in the design of the Bahamian flag symbolise the strength of the Bahamian people; the design reflects aspects of the natural environment (sun and sea) and the economic and social development. The flag is a black equilateral triangle against the mast, superimposed on a horizontal background made up of two colours on three equal stripes of aquamarine, gold and aquamarine.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_the_Bahamas" title="Coat of arms of the Bahamas">Coat of arms of the Bahamas</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_the_Bahamas.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1620" data-file-width="1323" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Coat_of_arms_of_the_Bahamas.svg/170px-Coat_of_arms_of_the_Bahamas.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Coat_of_arms_of_the_Bahamas.svg/255px-Coat_of_arms_of_the_Bahamas.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Coat_of_arms_of_the_Bahamas.svg/340px-Coat_of_arms_of_the_Bahamas.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_the_Bahamas.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nBahamian Coat of Arms</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The coat of arms of the Bahamas contains a shield with the national symbols as its focal point. The shield is supported by a <a href="/wiki/Marlin" title="Marlin">marlin</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Flamingo" title="Flamingo">flamingo</a>, which are the national animals of the Bahamas. The flamingo is located on the land, and the marlin on the sea, indicating the geography of the islands.</p>\n<p>On top of the shield is a conch shell, which represents the varied marine life of the island chain. The conch shell rests on a helmet. Below this is the actual shield, the main symbol of which is a ship representing the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_(ship)" title="Santa Maria (ship)">Santa Mar\xc3\xada</a></i> of Christopher Columbus, shown sailing beneath the sun. Along the bottom, below the shield appears a banner upon which is the national motto:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>\n<blockquote>\n<p><i>"Forward, Upward, Onward Together."</i></p>\n</blockquote>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_flower">National flower</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: National flower">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tecoma_stans" title="Tecoma stans">yellow elder</a> was chosen as the national flower of the Bahamas because it is native to the Bahama islands, and it blooms throughout the year.</p>\n<p>Selection of the yellow elder over many other flowers was made through the combined popular vote of members of all four of New Providence\'s garden clubs of the 1970s\xe2\x80\x94the Nassau Garden Club, the Carver Garden Club, the International Garden Club and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Young_Women%27s_Christian_Association" title="Young Women\'s Christian Association">Y.W.C.A.</a> Garden Club.</p>\n<p>They reasoned that other flowers grown there\xe2\x80\x94such as the <a href="/wiki/Bougainvillea" title="Bougainvillea">bougainvillea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hibiscus" title="Hibiscus">hibiscus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delonix_regia" title="Delonix regia">poinciana</a>\xe2\x80\x94had already been chosen as the national flowers of other countries. The yellow elder, on the other hand, was unclaimed by other countries (although it is now also the national flower of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a>) and also the yellow elder is native to the family islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Bahamas" title="Economy of the Bahamas">Economy of the Bahamas</a></div>\n<p>By <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP per capita">the terms of GDP per capita</a>, the Bahamas is one of the richest countries in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> It was revealed in the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Papers" title="Panama Papers">Panama Papers</a> that The Bahamas is the jurisdiction with the most offshore entities or companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICIJbahamas_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-ICIJbahamas-56">[56]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prince_George_Wharf_in_Nassau_Harbor.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="4000" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Prince_George_Wharf_in_Nassau_Harbor.jpg/300px-Prince_George_Wharf_in_Nassau_Harbor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Prince_George_Wharf_in_Nassau_Harbor.jpg/450px-Prince_George_Wharf_in_Nassau_Harbor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Prince_George_Wharf_in_Nassau_Harbor.jpg/600px-Prince_George_Wharf_in_Nassau_Harbor.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prince_George_Wharf_in_Nassau_Harbor.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cruise_ships" title="Cruise ships">Cruise ships</a> in Nassau Harbour</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Bahamas relies on <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> to generate most of its economic activity. Tourism as an industry not only accounts for over 60% of the Bahamian GDP, but provides jobs for more than half the country\'s workforce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The Bahamas attracted 5.8 million visitors in 2012, more than 70% of whom were cruise visitors.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services">Financial services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Financial services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>After tourism, the next most important economic sector is banking and international financial services, accounting for some 15% of GDP.</p>\n<p>The government has adopted incentives to encourage foreign financial business, and further banking and finance reforms are in progress. The government plans to merge the regulatory functions of key financial institutions, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_the_Bahamas" title="Central Bank of the Bahamas">Central Bank of the Bahamas</a> (CBB) and the Securities and Exchange Commission.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Central Bank administers restrictions and <a href="/wiki/Capital_control" title="Capital control">controls on capital</a> and money market instruments. The <a href="/wiki/Bahamas_Securities_Exchange" title="Bahamas Securities Exchange">Bahamas International Securities Exchange</a> consists of 19 listed public companies. Reflecting the relative soundness of the banking system (mostly populated by Canadian banks), the impact of the global financial crisis on the financial sector has been limited.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bahamas.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="865" data-file-width="1107" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Tree_map_export_2009_Bahamas.jpeg/350px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bahamas.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Tree_map_export_2009_Bahamas.jpeg/525px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bahamas.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Tree_map_export_2009_Bahamas.jpeg/700px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bahamas.jpeg 2x" width="350"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bahamas.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA proportional representation of the Bahamas exports.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The economy has a very competitive tax regime. The government derives its revenue from import tariffs, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VAT" title="VAT">VAT</a>, licence fees, property and stamp taxes, but there is no income tax, corporate tax, capital gains tax, or wealth tax. Payroll taxes fund social insurance benefits and amount to 3.9% paid by the employee and 5.9% paid by the employer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> In 2010, overall tax revenue as a percentage of GDP was 17.2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_the_Bahamas" title="Agriculture in the Bahamas">Agriculture in the Bahamas</a></div>\n<p>Agriculture is the third largest sector of the Bahamian economy, representing 5\xe2\x80\x937% of total GDP. An estimated 80% of the Bahamian food supply is imported. Major crops include <a href="/wiki/Onion" title="Onion">onions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Okra" title="Okra">okra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">oranges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grapefruit" title="Grapefruit">grapefruit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cucumber" title="Cucumber">cucumbers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lemon" title="Lemon">lemons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lime_(fruit)" title="Lime (fruit)">limes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">sweet potatoes</a>.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Bahamas" title="Demographics of the Bahamas">Demographics of the Bahamas</a></div>\n<p>The Bahamas has an estimated population of 391,232, of which 25.9% are under 14, 67.2% 15 to 64 and 6.9% over 65. It has a population growth rate of 0.925% (2010), with a birth rate of 17.81/1,000 population, death rate of 9.35/1,000, and net migration rate of \xe2\x88\x922.13 migrant(s)/1,000 population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rate</a> is 23.21 deaths/1,000 live births. Residents have a life expectancy at birth of 69.87 years: 73.49 years for females, 66.32 years for males. The total fertility rate is 2.0 children born/woman (2010).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The most populous islands are New Providence, where Nassau, the capital and largest city, is located;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> and Grand Bahama, home to the second largest city of <a href="/wiki/Freeport,_Bahamas" title="Freeport, Bahamas">Freeport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Racial_and_ethnic_groups">Racial and ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Racial and ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to the 99% response rate obtained from the race question on the 2010 Census questionnaire, 90.6% of the population identified themselves as being Black, 4.7% White and 2.1% of a mixed race (Black and White).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> according to the CIA Handbook. Other sources indicate whites number up to 12 to 15%, The Bahamas Guide, World Population Review. Three centuries prior, in 1722 when the first official census of the Bahamas was taken, 74% of the population was White and 26% Black.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soencouragement.org_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-soencouragement.org-62">[62]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gary_White_Visits_Local_Schools_-_Bahamas.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1856" data-file-width="3051" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Gary_White_Visits_Local_Schools_-_Bahamas.JPG/220px-Gary_White_Visits_Local_Schools_-_Bahamas.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Gary_White_Visits_Local_Schools_-_Bahamas.JPG/330px-Gary_White_Visits_Local_Schools_-_Bahamas.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Gary_White_Visits_Local_Schools_-_Bahamas.JPG/440px-Gary_White_Visits_Local_Schools_-_Bahamas.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gary_White_Visits_Local_Schools_-_Bahamas.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Afro-Bahamian" title="Afro-Bahamian">Afro-Bahamian</a> children at a local school</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Since the colonial era of plantations, Africans or Afro-Bahamians have been the largest ethnic group in the Bahamas, whose primary ancestry was based in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>. The first Africans to arrive to the Bahamas were freed slaves from <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>; they arrived with the <a href="/wiki/Eleutheran_Adventurers" title="Eleutheran Adventurers">Eleutheran Adventurers</a> looking for new lives.</p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haitian</a> community in the Bahamas is also largely of African descent and numbers about 80,000. Due to an extremely high immigration of Haitians to the Bahamas, the Bahamian government started deporting illegal Haitian immigrants to their homeland in late 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The White Bahamian population are mainly the descendants of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puritan" title="Puritan">English Puritans</a> looking to flee religious persecution in England and <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">American Loyalists</a> escaping the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_War_(United_States)" title="Revolutionary War (United States)">American Revolution</a> who arrived in 1649 and 1783, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Many Southern Loyalists went to the <a href="/wiki/Abaco_Islands" title="Abaco Islands">Abaco Islands</a>, half of whose population was of European descent as of 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The term <i>white</i> is usually used to identify Bahamians with Anglo ancestry, as well as "light-skinned" Afro-Bahamians. Sometimes Bahamians use the term <i>Conchy Joe</i> to describe people of Anglo descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Lesser-Known_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Lesser-Known-66">[66]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A small portion of the Euro-Bahamian population is descended from <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greek</a> labourers who came to help develop the sponging industry in the 1900s. They make up less than 1% of the nation\'s population, but have still preserved their distinct <a href="/wiki/Greek_Bahamians" title="Greek Bahamians">Greek Bahamian</a> culture.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<p>Bahamians typically identify themselves simply as either <i>black</i> or <i>white</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Lesser-Known_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Lesser-Known-66">[66]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of the Bahamas is English. Many people speak an <a href="/wiki/English-based_creole_languages" title="English-based creole languages">English-based creole language</a> called <i>Bahamian dialect</i> (known simply as "dialect") or "Bahamianese." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hackert_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hackert-67">[67]</a></sup> James Catalyn, a Bahamian writer and actor was the first to coin the latter name in a poem and has since promoted its usage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Both are used as autoglossonyms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">Haitian Creole</a>, a <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">French-based creole language</a> is spoken by Haitians and their descendants, who make up of about 25% of the total population. It is known simply as <i>Creole</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> to differentiate languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>Also note that the Bahamas was once under British rule and therefore the English taught in the Bahamian schools is still "British-based".</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Bahamas" title="Religion in the Bahamas">Religion in the Bahamas</a></div>\n<p>According to International Religious Freedom Report 2008 prepared by United States Bureau of Democracy, Human Rights and Labor, the islands\' population is predominantly <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> denominations are widespread and collectively account for more than 70% of the population, with <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> representing 35% of the population, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglicans" title="Anglicans">Anglicans</a> 15%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostals" title="Pentecostals">Pentecostals</a> 8%, <a href="/wiki/Church_of_God_(Holiness)" title="Church of God (Holiness)">Church of God</a> 5%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a> 5% and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methodists" title="Methodists">Methodists</a> 4%. There is also a significant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> community accounting for about 14%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-us-72">[72]</a></sup> There are also smaller communities of <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah\xc3\xa1\'\xc3\xad Faith">Baha\'is</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rastafari" title="Rastafari">Rastafarians</a> and practitioners of <a href="/wiki/Obeah" title="Obeah">Obeah</a>.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Bahamas" title="Culture of the Bahamas">Culture of the Bahamas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Bahamas" title="Music of the Bahamas">Music of the Bahamas</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Junkanoo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Junkanoo.jpg/220px-Junkanoo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Junkanoo.jpg/330px-Junkanoo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Junkanoo.jpg/440px-Junkanoo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Junkanoo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Junkanoo" title="Junkanoo">Junkanoo</a> celebration in <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">Nassau</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>In the less developed outer islands (or Family Islands), handicrafts include basketry made from palm fronds. This material, commonly called "straw", is plaited into hats and bags that are popular tourist items. Another use is for so-called "Voodoo dolls", even though such dolls are the result of the American imagination and not based on historic fact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>\n<p>A form of folk magic (<a href="/wiki/Obeah" title="Obeah">obeah</a>) is practiced by some Bahamians, mainly in the Family Islands (out-islands) of the Bahamas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The practice of obeah is illegal in the Bahamas and punishable by law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Junkanoo" title="Junkanoo">Junkanoo</a> is a traditional Afro-Bahamian street parade of \'rushing\', music, dance and art held in Nassau (and a few other settlements) every <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year\'s Day">New Year\'s Day</a>. Junkanoo is also used to celebrate other holidays and events such as Emancipation Day.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Regatta" title="Regatta">Regattas</a> are important social events in many family island settlements. They usually feature one or more days of sailing by old-fashioned <a href="/wiki/Boat" title="Boat">work boats</a>, as well as an onshore festival.</p>\n<p>Many dishes are associated with <a href="/wiki/Bahamian_cuisine" title="Bahamian cuisine">Bahamian cuisine</a>, which reflects Caribbean, African and European influences. Some settlements have festivals associated with the traditional crop or food of that area, such as the "Pineapple Fest" in Gregory Town, <a href="/wiki/Eleuthera" title="Eleuthera">Eleuthera</a> or the "Crab Fest" on Andros. Other significant traditions include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Story_telling" title="Story telling">story telling</a>.</p>\n<p>Bahamians have created a rich literature of poetry, short stories, plays and short fictional works. Common themes in these works are (1) an awareness of change, (2) a striving for sophistication, (3) a search for identity, (4) nostalgia for the old ways and (5) an appreciation of beauty. Some contributing writers are Susan Wallace, Percival Miller, Robert Johnson, Raymond Brown, O.M. Smith, William Johnson, Eddie Minnis and Winston Saunders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Bahamas culture is rich with beliefs, traditions, folklore and legend. The most well-known folklore and legends in the Bahamas includes Lusca in Andros Bahamas, Pretty Molly on Exuma Bahamas, the Chickcharnies of Andro Bahamas, and the Lost City of Atlantis on Bimini Bahamas.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Sport is a significant part of Bahamian culture. The national sport is <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a>. Cricket has been played in the Bahamas from 1846.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> It is the oldest sport being played in the country today. The <a href="/wiki/Bahamas_Cricket_Association" title="Bahamas Cricket Association">Bahamas Cricket Association</a> was formed in 1936 as an organised body. From the 1940s to the 1970s, cricket was played amongst many Bahamians. Bahamas is not a part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Indies_Cricket_Board" title="West Indies Cricket Board">West Indies Cricket Board</a>, so players are not eligible to play for the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies cricket team</a>. The late 1970s saw the game begin to decline in the country as teachers, who had previously come from the United Kingdom with a passion for cricket were replaced by teachers who had been trained in the United States. The Bahamian Physical education teachers had no knowledge of the game and instead taught <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track &amp; field</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> where primary and high schools compete against each other. Today cricket is still enjoyed by a few locals and immigrants in the country usually from <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>. Cricket is played on Saturdays and Sundays at Windsor Park and Haynes Oval.</p>\n<p>The only other sporting event that began before <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> was <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse racing</a>, which started in 1796. The most popular spectator sports are those imported from United States, such as <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> rather than Great Britain due to the country\'s close proximity to the United States. Unlike their other Caribbean counterparts, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a> have proven to be more popular.</p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Dexter_Cambridge" title="Dexter Cambridge">Dexter Cambridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Fox" title="Rick Fox">Rick Fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Lockhart" title="Ian Lockhart">Ian Lockhart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Hield" title="Buddy Hield">Buddy Hield</a> are a few Bahamians who joined Bahamian <a href="/wiki/Mychal_Thompson" title="Mychal Thompson">Mychal Thompson</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers" title="Los Angeles Lakers">Los Angeles Lakers</a> in the NBA ranks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Over the years <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> has become much more popular than <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>, though not implemented in the high school system yet. Leagues for teens and adults have been developed by the Bahamas American Football Federation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> However association football, commonly known as <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">\'soccer\'</a> in the country, is still a very popular sport amongst high school pupils. Leagues are governed by the <a href="/wiki/Bahamas_Football_Association" title="Bahamas Football Association">Bahamas Football Association</a>. Recently the Bahamian government has been working closely with <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> of London to promote the sport in the country as well as promoting the Bahamas in the European market. In 2013 \'Spurs\' became the first Premier League club to play an exhibition match in the Bahamas to face the <a href="/wiki/Jamaica_national_football_team" title="Jamaica national football team">Jamaica national football team</a>. <a href="/wiki/Joe_Lewis_(British_businessman)" title="Joe Lewis (British businessman)">Joe Lewis</a>, the owner of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur" title="Tottenham Hotspur">Tottenham Hotspur</a> club, is based in the Bahamas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Other popular sports are <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> where Bahamians have enjoyed some degree of success at the international level. Other sports such as <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Beach_soccer" title="Beach soccer">beach soccer</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a> are considered growing sports. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" title="Athletics (sport)">Athletics</a> commonly known as <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a> in the country is the most successful sport by far amongst Bahamians. Bahamians have a strong tradition in the <a href="/wiki/Sprint_(running)" title="Sprint (running)">sprints</a> and jumps. Track and field is probably the most popular spectator sport in the country next to <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> due to their success over the years. Triathlons are gaining popularity in Nassau and the Family Islands.</p>\n<p>Bahamians have gone on to win numerous <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a> medals at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Olympic_Games" title="The Olympic Games">the Olympic Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/IAAF_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="IAAF World Championships in Athletics">IAAF World Championships in Athletics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games" title="Pan American Games">Pan American Games</a>. <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rutherford" title="Frank Rutherford">Frank Rutherford</a> is the first athletics olympic medalist for the country. He won a bronze medal for triple jump during the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Summer Olympics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pauline_Davis-Thompson" title="Pauline Davis-Thompson">Pauline Davis-Thompson</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Debbie_Ferguson" title="Debbie Ferguson">Debbie Ferguson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chandra_Sturrup" title="Chandra Sturrup">Chandra Sturrup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Savatheda_Fynes" title="Savatheda Fynes">Savatheda Fynes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eldece_Clarke-Lewis" title="Eldece Clarke-Lewis">Eldece Clarke-Lewis</a> teamed up for the first athletics Olympic Gold medal for the country when they won the 4 \xc3\x97 100 m relay at the <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Summer Olympics</a>. They are affectionately known as the "Golden Girls".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tonique_Williams-Darling" title="Tonique Williams-Darling">Tonique Williams-Darling</a> became the first athletics individual Olympic gold medalist when she won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/400m" title="400m">400m</a> sprint in <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> In 2007, with the disqualification of <a href="/wiki/Marion_Jones" title="Marion Jones">Marion Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pauline_Davis-Thompson" title="Pauline Davis-Thompson">Pauline Davis-Thompson</a> was advanced to the gold medal position in the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2000_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_200_metres" title="Athletics at the 2000 Summer Olympics \xe2\x80\x93 Women\'s 200 metres">200 metres at the 2000 Olympics</a>, predating William-Darling.</p>\n<p>The Bahamas were hosts of the first men\'s senior FIFA tournament to be staged in the Caribbean, the <a href="/wiki/2017_FIFA_Beach_Soccer_World_Cup" title="2017 FIFA Beach Soccer World Cup">2017 FIFA Beach Soccer World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hostappointment_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hostappointment-99">[99]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Bahamas" title="Education in the Bahamas">Education in the Bahamas</a></div>\n<p>According to 1995 estimates 98.2% of the adult population is literate.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Representation_in_other_media">Representation in other media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Representation in other media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul>\n<li>Scenes from the final <i><a href="/wiki/Jaws_(film)" title="Jaws (film)">Jaws</a></i> movie (<i>Jaws: The Revenge</i>) were filmed on a New Providence Island beach now known as "Jaws Beach".</li>\n<li>The fourth official <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Bond_films" title="James Bond films">James Bond film</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Thunderball_(film)" title="Thunderball (film)">Thunderball</a></i> (1965), was partly filmed in <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">Nassau</a>, where much of the story is set. <a href="/wiki/Eon_Productions" title="Eon Productions">Eon Productions</a> were to return for filming underwater sequences in the famously clear waters, even when a Bond film\'s story was set elsewhere; for example, for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spy_Who_Loved_Me_(film)" title="The Spy Who Loved Me (film)">The Spy Who Loved Me</a></i> (1977).</li>\n<li>The unofficial remake of <i>Thunderball</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Never_Say_Never_Again" title="Never Say Never Again">Never Say Never Again</a></i> (1983), was similarly partly filmed in the islands, though this version of the story was not as extensively set there.</li>\n<li>The twenty-first official <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Bond_films" title="James Bond films">James Bond film</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(2006_film)" title="Casino Royale (2006 film)">Casino Royale</a></i> (2006), was in part set and filmed in the islands.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>\' film <i><a href="/wiki/Help!_(film)" title="Help! (film)">Help!</a></i> was filmed in part on New Providence Island and Paradise Island also in 1965.</li>\n<li>Nassau is featured in the 2013 video game <i><a href="/wiki/Assassin%27s_Creed_IV:_Black_Flag" title="Assassin\'s Creed IV: Black Flag">Assassin\'s Creed IV: Black Flag</a></i> as a pirate haven, housing the main protagonists. Historical pirates are encountered there such as <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Hornigold" title="Benjamin Hornigold">Benjamin Hornigold</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_Teach" title="Edward Teach">Edward Teach</a>/Blackbeard, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Vane" title="Charles Vane">Charles Vane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calico_Jack" title="Calico Jack">"Calico" Jack Rackham</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anne_Bonney" title="Anne Bonney">Anne Bonney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_Read" title="Mary Read">Mary Read</a>.</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bahamas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: See column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-cia.gov-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-cia.gov_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-cia.gov_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-cia.gov_1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-cia.gov_1-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a CIA World Factbook.</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-statistics-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-statistics_2-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://statistics.bahamas.gov.bs/download/095261300.pdf" rel="nofollow">Bahamas Department of Statistics</a>, PDF document retrieved 20 April 2014.</span></li>\n<li
